## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The target is the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) with respect to time, and the features are time (t) and concentration (A). This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the reaction rate is expressed as a function of the current concentration, and potentially explicit time dependence arises from non‑isothermal conditions or catalyst deactivation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero‑order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate of consumption)
- First‑order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (exponential decay of concentration)
- Second‑order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction)
- n‑th order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power‑law rate law)
- Fractional‑order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (chain reaction or half‑order kinetics)
- Time‑dependent rate constant (exponential decay): dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (decaying catalytic activity)
- Time‑dependent rate constant (power‑law decay): dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * t) (gradual deactivation)
- Reversible first‑order reaction: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (approach to equilibrium with positive c0, negative c1 relative to forward direction)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic‑type kinetics with self‑acceleration)
- Substrate inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * A + A**2) (enzyme or heterogeneous catalysis with inhibition)
- Coupled parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (mixed first‑ and second‑order contributions)
- Series reaction intermediate (via quasi‑steady state): dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) + c2 * A (Michaelis‑Menten with linear term)
- Temperature‑ramp equivalent rate (if t substitutes T): dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 / (t + c2)) (Arrhenius‑type time‑dependent activation)
- Diffusion‑controlled slow reaction: dA_dt = c0 / (t + c1)**0.5 (rate limited by time‑dependent diffusion layer)
- Oscillatory reaction (with time forcing): dA_dt = c0 * A * sin(c1 * t + c2) (periodic external modulation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Rate depends on current concentration raised to a power → reaction order (zero, first, second, fractional)
- If rate is proportional only to A, no explicit t → elementary rate law, time enters only through integration
- Explicit time dependence in dA/dt indicates a decaying rate constant (catalyst deactivation, non‑isothermal T(t))
- Autocatalysis gives a hump‑shaped rate vs A → product A*(A∞ - A)
- Enzyme or heterogeneous catalysis shows saturation at high A → rational form A/(constant + A)
- Inhibition by substrate or product introduces denominator terms with higher powers of A
- Reversible reactions yield an equilibrium point (dA/dt=0) → formula with two terms of opposite sign (linear combination)
- Fractional orders (e.g., 0.5) often arise from chain reactions or dissociative adsorption steps
- Diffusion‑limited regimes can introduce time‑dependent negative powers like t^(-1/2)
- Periodic or oscillatory kinetics require explicit trigonometric or oscillatory functions of t
